> **TIER: PROCESS / ARCHIVE.** Deliberation/meta; retained for rationale but NOT coherence-maintained as part of the 1.0 set. Roadmap index: docs/ROADMAP.md

# Determ — Formal proofs index

This directory contains the per-property analytic proofs for Determ's consensus, sharding, and slashing mechanisms. Each proof is self-contained: a theorem statement, the cryptographic and behavioral assumptions it depends on, the proof itself, and an implementation cross-reference so a reviewer can match the math to the code.

The proofs target two audiences:

1. **Protocol reviewers** — to confirm the properties Determ claims are actually proved, not assumed.
2. **Implementers** — to confirm each invariant is enforced at the exact source location the proof cites.

The proofs are written in standard mathematical prose, not in a machine-checkable spec language. A future track (FB) will add TLA+ models for the consensus and sharding state machines; the FA-track documents here are the human-readable counterpart.

---

## Reading order

Start with **F0 Preliminaries**. Everything else cites its notation, assumptions, and validity predicates.

| # | File | Property | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| F0 | [Preliminaries.md](Preliminaries.md) | Notation, assumptions, validity predicates | ✓ |
| FA1 | [Safety.md](Safety.md) | K-of-K mutual-distrust safety: ≤1 finalized digest per height. R39+2 B6 extended §7 (light-client safety composition) — **Theorem T-1.2** proves the trust-minimized `determ-light` never acts on data inconsistent with the operator's pinned genesis under adversary `A_daemon`, inheriting T-L1..T-L5 from LightClientThreatModel.md; **Corollary T-1.2.1** establishes fail-closed exit on any detected inconsistency. The light-client adds no new chain-level invariant — §7 composes the existing FA1 / FA-Apply / S-021 / S-033 / S-038 results into a per-invocation verifier. | ✓ |
| FA2 | [Censorship.md](Censorship.md) | Censorship resistance: union-tx-root inclusion of any honest mempool tx. R39+1 A6 extended §7 (F2 view-reconciliation composition — formalizes how the union-tx-root censorship bound survives the v2.7 F2 strict-determinism Phase-1 commitment under T-1 UnionMonotonic + T-3 OrderIndependent), §8 (S-014 rate-limiter interaction — composition with `net::RateLimiter` HELLO exemption + per-IP bucket independence so a single throttled adversary peer cannot starve honest tx admission), §9 (updated FA2 closure footing — restates the union-rule bound under the F2 + S-014 composition for v2.7 readiness) | ✓ |

| FA8-R | [ShardRoutingSoundness.md](ShardRoutingSoundness.md) | Address-to-shard routing primitive soundness (SR-0..SR-5 + SR-5.1) for `crypto::shard_id_for_address`: salt+count are chain-lifetime constants pinned into the genesis hash (SR-0, via S-039), determinism/chain-consistency — every node, wallet, and light client routes an address identically (SR-1), totality + partition — every address routes to exactly one in-range shard (SR-2), near-uniform load with modulo-bias `<= S·2⁻⁶⁴` under A3-ROM (SR-3), salt-binding / no cross-chain routing confusion under A2 + S-039 (SR-4), and misroute detection — the receiver recomputes `ρ` so producer + every receiver agree on `dst_shard` (SR-5), with routing-grind shown to be a non-attack against safety (SR-5.1). Discharges the `r.dst_shard == shard_id_for_address(tx.to, …)` premise that FA7 (`CrossShardReceipts.md` §61) and FA8 (`RegionalSharding.md` §3.4) cite without proof, and the "every address belongs to exactly one shard" premise FA-Apply-13 (`CrossShardOutboundApply.md` T-O4) + FA-Apply-17 (`CrossShardSupplyConservation.md`) rest on. 7-row adversary table (`A_nondeterm` / `A_orphan` / `A_starve` / `A_grind` / `A_misroute` / `A_crosschain` / `A_saltport`). Cites `src/crypto/random.cpp:177-191`, `src/chain/chain.cpp:198-201`, `src/chain/genesis.cpp:452`. Empirically pinned by `determ test-shard-routing-determinism` (`tools/test_shard_routing_determinism.sh`) + `determ test-shard-routing` baseline + `tools/test_anon_routing.sh` + `tools/test_chain_shard_routing_config.sh`. Sibling crypto-primitive proof to `MerkleTreeSoundness.md`. | ✓ |

Slashing-intersection clarification documents the FA6 boundary (evidence-driven slash predates UNSTAKE; locked decremented before the unlock-height refund path can fire). | ✓ |

| FA-Apply-9 | [CrossShardReceiptDedup.md](CrossShardReceiptDedup.md) | Cross-shard receipt dedup contract (T-R1..T-R7): first-application credits destination account and marks the `(origin_shard, receipt_hash)` pair-key in the dedup set (T-R1), duplicate application silently skips with no balance mutation and no nonce advance (T-R2), per-source-shard independence — dedup is keyed on the `(origin_shard, receipt_hash)` PAIR not the hash alone so identical receipt hashes originating from distinct source shards are NOT conflated (T-R3 — critical for K-shard correctness when hashes happen to collide across shards), snapshot serialize + restore preserves the `applied_inbound_receipts` set so post-restore replay correctly rejects already-applied receipts (T-R4 — companion to FA-Apply-2 + S-037), A1 unitary supply preserved across cross-shard composition — every inbound credit on shard D has a matching outbound debit on shard S in the K-shard set (T-R5 — companion to FA7), replay determinism — the dedup-check + credit-apply sequence is deterministic across replays of the same block ordering (T-R6), and the pre-application non-existence predicate (T-R7 — every credited receipt is provably absent from `applied_inbound_receipts` immediately before the credit step). The apply-layer cross-shard-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` CrossShardReceipt inbound-admission branches. | FA-Apply-10 | [EquivocationSlashingApply.md](EquivocationSlashingApply.md) | FA6 equivocation slashing apply-path contract (T-E1..T-E7) covering the chain.cpp apply-layer mechanics that close the loop between evidence detection (FA6) and chain-state effect: full forfeiture — slashing zeroes the offender's `stake_locked` and credits the entire amount to `accumulated_slashed` with no creator-side share (T-E1), registry deactivation — the slashed offender's `registrants_[d].active = false` flip happens in the same apply step so subsequent committee-selection rounds skip the domain (T-E2), idempotent re-apply — re-applying the same `EquivocationEvent` is a no-op (the second admission finds `stake_locked = 0` and the deactivation already set; FA6 evidence is replay-safe at the apply layer) (T-E3), ghost-evidence robustness — `EquivocationEvent` targeting a domain absent from `stakes_` / `registrants_` silently no-ops without violating A1 (T-E4), A1 invariance — slashing converts `stake_locked` → `accumulated_slashed`; both are tracked under the unitary-supply identity, so the per-apply invariant `live_total_supply + accumulated_slashed = expected_total` is preserved (T-E5), cross-block accumulation — multiple equivocation events across different blocks each contribute their per-event slash amount additively to `accumulated_slashed`, with no per-domain stacking beyond the first event's full forfeiture (T-E6), and determinism across replays — replaying the same block sequence (chain reload, snapshot restore + re-apply) produces byte-identical `accumulated_slashed` + `stakes_` + `registrants_` state (T-E7). The apply-layer slashing-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` EquivocationEvent apply branch. Cross-references `tools/test_equivocation_slashing.sh` + `determ test-equivocation-apply` + `determ test-equivocation-multi` regressions. Companion analytic to FA6 (which proves slashing soundness at the evidence-detection layer); FA-Apply-10 covers the apply-path mechanics conditional on FA6's evidence soundness. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-11 | [AbortEventApply.md](AbortEventApply.md) | AbortEvent apply-path contract (T-A1..T-A8) covering the chain.cpp apply-layer mechanics for the FA5 selective-abort defense: Phase-1 proportional slash — Round-1 abort events trigger proportional `stake_locked` debit per the protocol's anti-cartel formula, with the slashed amount credited to `accumulated_slashed` (T-A1), Phase-2 no-slash semantics — Round-2 abort events propagate as informational evidence only (no stake mutation; FA5 covers the protocol-design rationale — Round-2 aborts indicate honest disagreement on a Byzantine input rather than provable misbehavior) (T-A2), no registry deactivation — unlike EquivocationEvent (FA-Apply-10), AbortEvent does NOT flip `registrants_[d].active = false`; the offender's domain remains in the active set on subsequent committee selections, matching the protocol's "abort is recoverable, equivocation is terminal" distinction (T-A3), A1 invariance — Phase-1 slashing converts `stake_locked` → `accumulated_slashed`; A1 unitary-supply identity preserved across both Phase-1 (slash) and Phase-2 (no-op) branches (T-A4), idempotent re-apply — re-applying the same Phase-1 `AbortEvent` finds the prior slash already committed (`stake_locked` already decremented; replay-safe) (T-A5), ghost-evidence robustness — Phase-1 AbortEvent targeting a domain absent from `stakes_` silently no-ops without violating A1 (T-A6), per-block accumulation — multiple Phase-1 events in a single block each contribute additively to `accumulated_slashed` via the block-level `block_slashed` accumulator (T-A7), and determinism across replays — replaying the same block sequence produces byte-identical `accumulated_slashed` + `stakes_` + `registrants_` state across chain reload + snapshot restore + re-apply (T-A8). Apply-layer abort-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` AbortEvent apply branch. Cross-references `tools/test_abort_event_apply` + the abort-flow integration regressions in `tools/test_*.sh`. Companion analytic to FA5 (which proves selective-abort defense soundness at the evidence-detection layer); FA-Apply-11 covers the apply-path mechanics conditional on FA5's evidence soundness. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-12 | [AppliedReceiptRestore.md](AppliedReceiptRestore.md) | Cross-shard `applied_inbound_receipts` dedup-set restore correctness contract (T-R1..T-R5): snapshot serialization includes the dedup-set in the `r:` namespace and the S-033 state_root binds it (T-R1 — via S-037 producer-side wiring + S-038 state_root population), restore re-installs the dedup-set into the destination shard's chain state byte-for-byte (T-R2), post-restore `apply_block` rejects any inbound receipt whose `(origin_shard, origin_block, receipt_hash)` triple is already present in the restored set (T-R3 — the FA7 no-double-credit invariant must survive snapshot bootstrap), idempotent restore under repeated invocation (T-R4 — restoring the same snapshot twice yields byte-identical dedup-set state), and A1 unitary-supply invariance — restoring the dedup-set preserves the cross-shard receipt-flow accounting that FA7 relies on (T-R5). The apply-layer post-snapshot-restore replay-defense invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` snapshot restore + cross-shard receipt admission branches. Cross-references `tools/test_cross_shard_atomicity` + `tools/test_snapshot_bootstrap` + `tools/test_dapp_snapshot` regressions; companion to FA-Apply-2 (snapshot equivalence) and FA7 (cross-shard receipt soundness) — FA-Apply-12 closes the conditional that FA-Apply-2's apply-after-restore equivalence holds *across* the cross-shard receipt-dedup invariant, which neither FA-Apply-2 nor FA7 alone covers. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-14 | [NefPoolDrain.md](NefPoolDrain.md) | E1 Negative-Entry-Fee (NEF) `nef_pool` drain apply-path contract (T-N1..T-N7) covering the chain.cpp economic-bootstrap mechanics for the first-time-REGISTER subsidy: per-REGISTER geometric drain — first-time `REGISTER` triggers exactly one `nef_pool / 2` payout credited to the registrant's `balance`, then `nef_pool` halves to `floor(nef_pool / 2)` (T-N1), no-double-drain on update-REGISTER — re-REGISTER of an already-active domain (or any REGISTER hitting an existing registry entry) emits no NEF credit and does not mutate `nef_pool` (T-N2), pool-exhaustion safety — when `nef_pool == 0` or has decayed to single-unit dust, subsequent first-time REGISTERs still succeed but mint zero (the registry side-effect proceeds independently of the NEF subsidy stream) (T-N3), per-registrant independence — each fresh domain that registers for the first time gets its own `nef_pool / 2` slice of the then-current pool, with the geometric series 1/2 + 1/4 + 1/8 + ... bounded above by the genesis-configured `nef_pool_initial` (T-N4), A1 invariance — NEF drain converts `nef_pool` → `registrant.balance`; both are tracked under the unitary-supply identity, so the per-apply invariant `live_total_supply + accumulated_slashed = expected_total` is preserved across REGISTER apply (T-N5), idempotent re-apply under restore — replaying the same chain-tail after `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` reproduces byte-identical `nef_pool` + per-account `balance` state because the genesis `nef_pool_initial` and the registry's `registered_at` field together pin down the drain history (T-N6), and determinism across replays — replaying the same block sequence (chain reload, snapshot restore + re-apply) produces byte-identical `nef_pool` + balances + `registrants_` state (T-N7). The apply-layer NEF-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` REGISTER first-time-only NEF branch. Cross-references `tools/test_nef_pool_drain.sh` + `determ test-nef-pool-drain` regressions. Companion analytic to FA11 (which proves A1 unitary-supply invariance at the economic-soundness layer); FA-Apply-14 covers the apply-path mechanics of the E1 NEF subsidy stream that FA11 cites as one of the bounded inflation channels. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-13 | [CrossShardOutboundApply.md](CrossShardOutboundApply.md) | Source-side cross-shard `TRANSFER` apply-path contract (T-O1..T-O8) covering the chain.cpp source-shard mechanics for the cross-shard transfer flow (companion to FA-Apply-9 which covers the destination-side credit + dedup): cross-shard detection — `is_cross_shard(from, to)` short-circuits on single-shard mode and delegates to `shard_id_for_address` salt-aware routing on multi-shard mode (T-O1), source-side debit — sender's `balance` is decremented by `amount + fee` before any outbound-receipt emission (no balance escapes the source shard without a paired debit) (T-O2), outbound receipt emission — the apply-step records a `CrossShardReceipt {origin_shard = my_shard_id, origin_block, dest_shard, from, to, amount, receipt_hash}` into the source shard's `outbound_receipts_` queue with the canonical hash derived from `(origin_shard, origin_block, from, to, amount, nonce)` (T-O3), `dest_shard` derivation correctness — `dest_shard = shard_id_for_address(to, shard_count, shard_address_salt)` matches the destination's `my_shard_id` for FA7 atomicity to hold across the K-shard set (T-O4), nonce advance — sender's `next_nonce` is incremented exactly once per outbound `TRANSFER` (same contract as the same-shard branch; FA-Apply-3 nonce-monotonicity invariant) (T-O5), A1 invariance — outbound emission converts `source.balance` → `outbound_receipts_` queue (intra-K-shard supply identity preserved; companion to FA7 cross-shard composition theorem) (T-O6), idempotent re-apply across snapshot restore — replaying the same source-shard block after `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` produces byte-identical `balance` + `outbound_receipts_` + `next_nonce` state (T-O7 — companion to FA-Apply-12 which covers the destination's `applied_inbound_receipts` set), and determinism across replays — replaying the same block sequence (chain reload, snapshot restore + re-apply) produces byte-identical source-shard chain state (T-O8). The apply-layer source-side cross-shard-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` `TRANSFER` cross-shard branch + outbound-receipt-emission step. Cross-references `tools/test_cross_shard_transfer.sh` + `tools/test_cross_shard_atomicity.sh` + `determ test-cross-shard-outbound-apply` regressions. Companion analytic to FA-Apply-9 (destination-side credit + dedup) and FA7 (cross-shard atomicity proof — the K-shard sum identity rests on the source-side debit-then-emit invariant proven here). | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-15 | [MultiEventComposition.md](MultiEventComposition.md) | Multi-event composition theorem in `apply_transactions` (T-M1..T-M6) covering the **joint** apply-path property when a single finalized block carries a heterogeneous mix of state-mutating surfaces — ordinary transactions, `AbortEvent`s, `EquivocationEvent`s, and `CrossShardReceipt` inbound entries — together with the per-block accumulators (`block_inbound`, `block_outbound`, `block_slashed`, `total_fees`, `subsidy_this_block`) that feed the A1 closure: per-surface invariants compose without cross-surface interference because each loop body writes to a disjoint state-map subset (T-M1), the deterministic apply order is consensus-pinned and order-independent in the chain-wide accumulators by `u64` commutativity (T-M2), A1 unitary-supply identity holds additively over per-surface deltas, so multi-event blocks preserve `live_total_supply + accumulated_slashed = expected_total` provided each individual FA-Apply-* invariant holds in isolation (T-M3), S-033 state_root binds the post-apply state of all surfaces simultaneously because every namespace (a:/s:/r:/d:/i:/b:/m:/p:/k:/c:) appears in `compute_state_root` and the producer-side wiring (S-038) populates `body.state_root` on every block regardless of event mix (T-M4), snapshot replay equivalence (T-S2 from FA-Apply-2) composes — re-applying the same multi-event block after `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` yields byte-identical state across all surfaces because each surface's dedup-set / accumulator / balance map is round-tripped independently (T-M5), and determinism — replaying the same multi-event block sequence produces byte-identical chain state across every surface (T-M6). The composition is structural rather than mechanical: it rests on the apply path being a finite sequence of independent loops, each body reading from + writing to a disjoint state-map subset (modulo `accounts_[d]` touched by both `TRANSFER` recipients and `DAPP_CALL` recipients, both of which only mutate `balance` + `next_nonce`), with the chain-wide accumulators acting as the linear-superposition channel that the apply-tail A1 closure consumes as a single ledger equation. Companion analytic that consolidates FA-Apply-1 through FA-Apply-14 into a single joint-correctness theorem; FA-Apply-15 covers the multi-event block case that none of the per-surface FA-Apply proofs covers in isolation. Cross-references `tools/test_block_event_composition.sh` + `tools/test_multi_event_apply.sh` + the apply-path regressions in `tools/test_*.sh`. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-16 | [StakeForfeitureCascade.md](StakeForfeitureCascade.md) | Stake forfeiture cascade theorem (T-C1..T-C7) covering the **cascading apply-path interaction** between EquivocationEvent slashing (FA-Apply-10), AbortEvent slashing (FA-Apply-11), and post-slash registry deactivation across a single block + across chained blocks where the same offender triggers multiple slash events: full-forfeiture monotonicity — once `EquivocationEvent` zeroes `stake_locked` for domain `d`, subsequent same-block or future-block `AbortEvent` against `d` finds `stake_locked = 0` and silently no-ops (the Phase-1 proportional debit's `min(stake, slash_amount)` gate; replay-safe by construction; T-C1), deactivation cascade — the EquivocationEvent's `registrants_[d].active = false` flip in the same apply step propagates to all subsequent committee-selection rounds, so cascading slash events against the now-deactivated domain are admissible at the apply layer (no `is_registered` precondition is checked at the slash branch) but produce no further state mutation because `stake_locked = 0` and `registrants_[d]` is already inactive (T-C2), accumulated_slashed monotonicity — the chain-wide `accumulated_slashed` accumulator grows monotonically across cascade events (no double-counting; each event's contribution is `min(prev_stake, slash_amount)` so subsequent events on a zeroed stake add zero; T-C3), A1 invariance under cascade — multiple slash events against the same offender preserve the unitary-supply identity because the conversion `stake_locked → accumulated_slashed` is one-shot at the first event; cascaded events convert `0 → 0` (T-C4), per-block accumulation — cascade events in a single block sum additively into `block_slashed` without per-domain stacking beyond the first event's full forfeiture; the `block_slashed` accumulator is the apply-tail closure point that FA-Apply-15 composes (T-C5), snapshot replay equivalence — replaying a cascade across `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` produces byte-identical `accumulated_slashed` + per-domain `stake_locked` + `registrants_[d].active` state across the cascade chain (T-C6), and determinism — replaying the same cascade block sequence (chain reload, snapshot restore + re-apply) produces byte-identical state across all surfaces (T-C7). The apply-layer cascade-correctness invariant tracked against `chain.cpp` EquivocationEvent + AbortEvent apply branches under the cascading-offender case. Cross-references `tools/test_equivocation_multi.sh` + `tools/test_equivocation_slashing.sh` + `determ test-equivocation-apply` regressions. Companion analytic to FA-Apply-10 (equivocation slash) + FA-Apply-11 (abort slash); FA-Apply-16 covers the cascading-interaction case where the same offender triggers multiple slash events in close succession — neither FA-Apply-10 nor FA-Apply-11 alone covers the post-zero-stake replay-safety contract that FA-Apply-16's T-C1 + T-C2 pin down. | ✓ |
| FA-Apply-17 | [CrossShardSupplyConservation.md](CrossShardSupplyConservation.md) | K-shard aggregate supply-conservation theorem (XS-1..XS-5): the multi-shard composition of the per-shard A1 unitary-supply invariant into a single closed identity over the whole K-shard set — `Σ_shards (Σ balances + Σ staked + outbound_in_flight) + Σ accumulated_slashed = Σ genesis_total`. Per-step conservation — every cross-shard apply step (source debit + `accumulated_outbound +=` emit, destination credit + `accumulated_inbound +=`) preserves the aggregate because each shard's contribution algebraically collapses to its constant `genesis_total` (XS-1); no double-credit ⇒ no inflation — the FA-Apply-9 dedup guard makes a replayed inbound receipt a no-op, so `accumulated_inbound` increments exactly once per emitted receipt (key uniqueness under A2 SHA-256 collision resistance; the `(src_shard, tx_hash)` pair-key) and conservation survives gossip/replay duplication (XS-2); fee handling — the cross-shard fee stays on the source shard (booked into `total_fees` → creator distribution within the same `live_total_supply`, never into `accumulated_outbound`), so it never escapes the aggregate (XS-3, composes FA-Apply-6 T-F6); snapshot-restore invariance — `serialize_state`→`restore_from_snapshot` round-trips all seven supply-bearing fields + the `applied_inbound_receipts` dedup set (and back-solves `genesis_total` for legacy snapshots via the rearranged A1 identity), so the aggregate is identical post-restore (XS-4, composes FA-Apply-2 T-S3 + FA-Apply-12 T-R4); aggregate identity — induction over apply steps (genesis base case `live = genesis_total`, XS-1..XS-4 as the inductive step) concludes `TotalSupply = Σ genesis_total` for every reachable multi-shard state (XS-5). The A-number namespace is explicit: "A1" here is the apply-layer accounting identity per `Preliminaries.md` §2.0, NOT cryptographic A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA). Consolidation proof — the cross-shard generalization that none of the per-shard/per-receipt proofs (FA-Apply-1/9/13, FA7) states as one closed equation over the K-shard set. Bounded to one deployment (cross-deployment bridges are v2.23) and conditional on honest apply (Byzantine block content caught by V12/V13 + FA1 + S-033). Empirically pinned by sibling D1's `determ test-cross-shard-supply-invariant` (commit `7ee49da`; `tools/test_cross_shard_supply_invariant.sh`; 30 PASS) across a K=3 shard set with a non-zero staked term, mid-cycle (coin in flight) and post-credit, with a duplicate-inbound no-op assertion and a snapshot round-trip. D1's `aggregate_conserved()` lambda uses `accumulated_outbound()` as the source-side in-flight signal — there is no `outbound_receipts_` member. Companion to FA7 (per-receipt exactly-once delivery), FA-Apply-1 (per-shard A1), FA-Apply-9/13 (destination/source apply mechanics), FA-Apply-2/12 (snapshot equivalence). | ✓ |
| FA-Cert | [AbortCertificateSoundness.md](AbortCertificateSoundness.md) | Abort-certificate quorum-verification soundness (V10 / `check_abort_certs`) — the verification-side bookend to FA6 for the abort accusation channel; proves an honest validator is never falsely suspension-slashed. Seven theorems T-C1..T-C7: membership soundness — honest non-member is never named (V10 re-derives the at-event committee and rejects `aborting_node ∉ domains_at_event`; T-C1), producer/validator committee-re-derivation agreement — the V10 seed chain is byte-identical to V3 so honest nodes never disagree on at-event membership (T-C2), quorum-signature soundness — fabricating an `M−1` certificate against honest `d` requires forging an honest claimer's Ed25519 sig over the domain-separated `make_abort_claim_message(h, round, prev_hash, d)` digest, `≤ q·2⁻¹²⁸` under EUF-CMA + honest-majority committee (T-C3), domain separation — abort claims are non-replayable across round / height / missing-creator / fork / other message spaces via the four per-field rejects + A2 (T-C4), exact-count + distinct-claimer enforcement — `!=` count reject + `seen_claimers` set + `claimer == missing_creator` reject defeat quorum-padding and self-claim (T-C5), phase discrimination preserved — V10 admits round-1 and round-2 aborts identically; the Phase-1-slash / Phase-2-informational asymmetry lives in the apply layer only (T-C6), and determinism + snapshot-stability of the verdict (T-C7). 8-row adversary table (`A_nonmember` / `A_seed_grind` / `A_forge_claim` / `A_replay` / `A_pad` / `A_self_claim` / `A_phase_smuggle` / `A_full_byzantine_committee`). §3 contrasts the two accusation channels: abort = third-party attestation (needs committee-membership binding + honest-majority committee), equivocation = self-incrimination (committee-agnostic, unconditional in `f`). Closes the V10-soundness dependency that `AbortEventApply.md` (FA-Apply-11) §4 explicitly defers. Cites `src/node/validator.cpp:172-298` (`check_abort_certs`), `src/chain/chain.cpp:1314` (apply-side round gate), `include/determ/node/producer.hpp:67-82` (`AbortClaimMsg` + `make_abort_claim_message`), `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:228-237` (`AbortEvent`). Cross-references `tools/test_abort_reselection.sh` + `tools/test_abort_event_apply.sh` + `determ test-block-validator-extensive`. Companion to FA6 (`EquivocationSlashing.md`), FA-Apply-11 (`AbortEventApply.md`), FA5 (`SelectiveAbort.md`), S-020 (`S020CommitteeSelection.md`), S-013 (`S013PerSignerCap.md`). | ✓ |
| FA-Phase | [ConsensusPhaseStructureSoundness.md](ConsensusPhaseStructureSoundness.md) | Two-phase per-block consensus structural soundness: Phase-1 commit determinism + commit-set agreement (T-1), Phase-1→Phase-2 SHA-256 second-preimage binding of dh_secret to dh_input (T-2), pure-function determinism of delay_seed/delay_output/cumulative_rand with validator re-derivation match (T-3), and the K-arrived phase-transition gate ensuring Phase-2 signing only over a sealed ordered commitment set in both modes (T-4). | FA-CSAD | [CommitteeSelectionAbortDeterminismSoundness.md](CommitteeSelectionAbortDeterminismSoundness.md) | Abort-driven committee re-selection is deterministic across honest nodes (T-1..T-4): the abort list is canonically ordered (`std::vector` index order, identically observed via the block's serialized `abort_events`; T-1), the seed-mixing recurrence `rand_{i+1} = SHA256(rand_i ‖ ae_i.event_hash)` from base `epoch_committee_seed(epoch_rand, shard_id)` is a byte-identical pure function of the shared abort history with NO cryptographic assumption (T-2; order-sensitivity is shared-not-divergent per T-2.1, the only A2 term), composing with S-020 T-5 sampler determinism to give end-to-end byte-identical committees so the validator V3 gate (`check_creator_selection`) accepts exactly the producer's committee and abort handling introduces no honest fork (T-3), hence a Byzantine abort-grinder moves the committee identically for everyone (grind-invariance; T-4) — the grinding-PAYOFF bound (uniformity, bounded rounds, slashing cost) is explicitly delegated to Censorship.md / Liveness.md / AbortEventApply.md. | FB-OE | [OfflineEquivocationEvidenceSoundness.md](OfflineEquivocationEvidenceSoundness.md) | Offline `determ-light` equivocation-evidence verifier: adjudicates two conflicting signed messages from one signer at the same (height,generation) against the V11 predicate with no network/chain state, under fabricating-accuser `A_accuser`. | FB-DC | [DAppRegistryCommitmentSoundness.md](DAppRegistryCommitmentSoundness.md) | `d:`-leaf encoding injectivity + the registry/message commitment-coverage boundary for the v2.18/v2.19 DApp subsystem. DC-1: the leaf-value encoding `enc_d : DAppEntry → bytes` is a fully length-prefixed (TLV) serialization (32-byte pubkey ‖ three u64 lifecycle anchors ‖ u64-prefixed endpoint_url ‖ u64-count topic vector with per-topic u64 prefixes ‖ u8→u64 retention ‖ u64-prefixed metadata), hence injective — so under A2 a passing `d:` inclusion proof binds the verifier to exactly one `DAppEntry` field-tuple (no field-boundary smuggling; the value-side analogue of MT-2 key domain separation). DC-2: `enc_d` is total (empty endpoint / zero topics / empty metadata / `inactive_from = UINT64_MAX` sentinel) + deterministic across replay + snapshot restore (unconditional). DC-3: every field `rpc_dapp_info`/`rpc_dapp_list` returns is `state_root`-committed via the single `d:` leaf, so those answers are succinctly trustless against the committee-signed `state_root` (specializes S-033 T-1 + LightClientThreatModel T-L3). DC-4 (the novel boundary): NO `DAPP_CALL` payload byte enters `enc_d` or any of the 10 `state_root` namespaces — the message stream is committed only by per-block `tx_root`, so a `rpc_dapp_messages` page is per-tx-sound (verify each `tx_hash` against the enclosing block's committee-signed `tx_root`, the `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md` surface, A1+A2) but only block-availability-complete: a Byzantine daemon may omit/truncate/reorder a page without contradicting any `state_root` proof. Lemma DC-K: `d:` is a simple ASCII namespace (key `"d:"‖domain`), so the hex-transport boundary `StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md` secures for the composite `i:`/`m:`/`p:` namespaces does not arise. 7-row adversary table (`A_value_collide` / `A_field_smuggle` / `A_retention_overflow` / `A_key_alias` / `A_msg_fabricate` / `A_msg_omit` / `A_root_confuse`) whose load-bearing rows are the honest negative results `A_msg_omit` + `A_root_confuse` — the DApp message stream does NOT inherit the registry entry's succinct trustless-read guarantee. Reduces to A2 (DC-1), unconditional (DC-2), A1+A2 (DC-3/DC-4). Cites `src/chain/chain.cpp:312-329` (`enc_d`), `src/crypto/sha256.cpp:30-34` (8-byte big-endian `append(uint64_t)`), `src/node/node.cpp:2987-3120` (`rpc_dapp_info`/`rpc_dapp_list`/`rpc_dapp_messages`), `node.cpp:3314` (`d:` in the simple-namespace `state_proof` branch), `chain.cpp:1118-1175` (`DAPP_CALL` apply touches only `a:` balances/nonces + `total_fees`, stores no payload in chain state). Orthogonal to FA-Apply-5 (`DAppRegistryLifecycle.md`, apply-layer state machine); companion to `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md`, `StakeProofSoundness.md`, `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md`, `MerkleTreeSoundness.md`, `StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md`, `LightClientThreatModel.md`. Exercised indirectly by `tools/test_dapp_register.sh` + `tools/test_dapp_state_transition.sh` + `tools/test_dapp_snapshot.sh` + `tools/test_state_root_determinism.sh`. | ✓ |

| [FrostVerifyDelegation.md](FrostVerifyDelegation.md) | v2.10 Phase A soundness proof for `src/crypto/frost.cpp::frost_verify`. Theorem T-1 (verification soundness): a `frost_verify(sig, group_pubkey, msg)` call returns TRUE iff `sig` is a valid t-of-K FROST aggregation over `msg` under `group_pubkey`, by reduction through L-1 (RFC 9591 §5.1 aggregate ∈ Ed25519 sig space) + L-2 (`determ::crypto::verify` wraps EVP_PKEY_ED25519). | [FrostThresholdSoundness.md](FrostThresholdSoundness.md) | **[FROST block-beacon application DE-SCOPED — MPDH commit-reveal retained; proof stands as a signature-scheme result. FROST is removed from the v1.1 chain consensus path entirely (FROST_DEVIATION_NOTICE.md); FROST C99 is library-only. See the doc's STATUS.]** **Construction-soundness companion** to the implementation audits (C99CryptoStackAudit §6/§7/§8/§8b), extending FrostVerifyDelegation from the one old `frost_verify` primitive to the now-shipped C99 FROST keygen / threshold signing / DKG (`src/crypto/{ed25519,frost}/`). Seven theorems under A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA) / A2 (DL) / A3 (SHA-512 RO) / A4 (honest dealer ∨ honest-participant DKG): **T-1** the t-of-n aggregate satisfies the Ed25519 verify equation `[z]B = R + [c]·PK` (so it IS a standard Ed25519 signature — `r = Σ(dᵢ+ρᵢeᵢ)`, `z = r + c·s`, `Σλᵢ(0)sᵢ = f(0) = s`); **T-1.1** the distributed two-round split shipped in `b49db4f` (`determ_frost_sign_partial` per-signer round-2 + `determ_frost_aggregate`, the shape Phase D consumes) is byte-identical to the centralized `determ_frost_sign` because all three share one binding/`R`/challenge derivation — asserted by `test-frost-c99` `memcmp(...)==0`; **T-2** Shamir reconstruction correctness + `<t` information-theoretic secrecy; **T-3** threshold EUF-CMA by reduction to the FROST literature (Komlo–Goldberg 2020; the message-and-commitment-bound binding factor `ρᵢ` is the Drijvers/ROS concurrent-signing defence); **T-4** the DKG never assembles `s` in one place + Feldman VSS binding (`[s]B = Σ jᵏ·Cᵢ,ₖ` ⟺ `s ≡ f_i(j)`, cheating dealer caught modulo DL); **T-5** the Schnorr proof-of-possession is a sound PoK of `a_{i,0}` (forking-lemma extraction), with `idx`-binding as the rogue-key defence and the deterministic nonce shown benign; **T-6** the PSS refresh shipped in `090931f` (`determ_frost_pss_commit` zero-hole Feldman commitments + `determ_frost_pss_verify_commit` enforcing `C_0=[0]B`) rotates every share under the UNCHANGED group key — refreshed shares lie on `g=f+Δ` with `Δ(0)=Σδ_i(0)=0` so `g(0)=s` is preserved, share *values* move, and an old+new cross-epoch mix interpolates to `s''≠s` (mobile-adversary defence), witnessed by `test-frost-c99` §6; **T-7** committee-lifecycle composition — the DKG group key `PK` is a cross-epoch INVARIANT (induction over PSS refreshes: each preserves `f(0)=s` so `PK_e=PK₀`), every signing epoch yields standard Ed25519 sigs under that one fixed `PK`, and selective-abort resistance holds per-epoch — so a light client that pins `PK₀` once validates every signature the committee ever produces across all refreshes + handovers (the contract the v2.10 consensus wiring + light-client beacon verification rely on). §4 explains what each canonicality gate buys (signer-set guard, `S<L`, `y<q` — uniqueness/non-malleability, not knowledge-soundness). §5 scopes the non-goals: RFC-9591 byte-exact interop deferred, implementation-correctness + constant-time delegated to the audits, consensus wiring out of scope. Cross-refs C99CryptoStackAudit §6/§7/§8/§8b, FrostVerifyDelegation, CRYPTO-C99-SPEC §3.2/§3.8, V210ImplementationRoadmap, `test-ed25519-c99`/`test-frost-c99`. |
| [V210ImplementationRoadmap.md](V210ImplementationRoadmap.md) | **[block-beacon DE-SCOPED — MPDH retained. FROST is removed from the v1.1 chain consensus path entirely (FROST_DEVIATION_NOTICE.md); FROST C99 is library-only.]** Verified v2.10 (FROST-Ed25519 threshold randomness) scoping roadmap (no code change). Implemented-vs-stubbed map (only `frost_verify` real; keygen/sign/aggregate throw `v2.10 Phase A not yet implemented` in `src/crypto/frost.cpp`). **The load-bearing finding (§2):** no Ed25519 scalar/point backend is linked into the `determ` daemon — OpenSSL `EVP_PKEY_ED25519` exposes only high-level sign/verify; libsodium is vendored but linked only into `determ-wallet`/`oprf` (`determ-light` explicitly excludes it); `src/crypto/ed25519/` does not exist; and `frost.cpp` calls no group-op function. **Three in-tree docs name three mutually-exclusive backends** (libsodium per `frost.hpp:15-16`; independent `ref10` per `v2.10-DKG-SPEC.md`; libsodium-free per `CRYPTO-C99-SPEC.md`). So Phase A WAS **BLOCKED-ON-PREREQ** — now **RESOLVED** (commit `031be9e`): `src/crypto/ed25519/ed25519.c` is a from-scratch, constant-time, libsodium-free Ed25519 (RFC 8032) in the TweetNaCl-derived `gf[16]` representation, validated byte-equal vs OpenSSL `EVP_PKEY_ED25519` + the RFC 8032 §7.1 KAT by `determ test-ed25519-c99` (preserves the `determ-light` libsodium-free invariant; the chosen path over both libsodium-linking and `ref10`). The next P0 is now the FROST primitives (keygen/sign/aggregate) on this group-op layer, not the backend. The smallest-safe increment (`test-frost-vectors`: scalar-field + H1..H5 against RFC 9591 / RFC 8032 known-answer vectors) is GO once a backend is wired — additive, zero consensus-path touch, does not flip the `v2_10_active_from_height` gate (v1 commit-reveal path intact below activation). |

| [S014RateLimiterSoundness.md](S014RateLimiterSoundness.md) | S-014 token-bucket rate-limiter soundness for per-peer-IP RPC + gossip rate limiting. Six theorems T-1 (Bounded Burst: per-IP allowed count ≤ capacity + rate × Δ over any window), T-2 (No DoS Amplification: constant-time per-request rejection cost), T-3 (Per-IP Independence), T-4 (HELLO Exemption Safety: HELLO size-bounded + idempotent), T-5 (Refill Monotonicity: no underflow under clock skew), T-6 (Capacity vs Rate Trade-off per profile). Seven lemmas L-1..L-7. §6 surfaces three findings: **F-1 (Low): unbounded `buckets_` growth** — ✅ CLOSED via time-decay eviction in `configure_eviction()` + amortized sweep on consume hot path; defaults 600s/60s with ≥60× safety margin over realistic refill time; semantic-equivalence preserved by resurrection-safe re-creation. F-2 (Very Low): steady_clock epoch-0 sentinel defense-in-depth. F-3 (Low): no per-method weighting on RPC. References RFC 2475, RFC 2697, Cruz 1991, Le Boudec-Thiran 2001. **R39+ round-2 §9 re-cap** explicitly restates the soundness conclusions under the `RL-N` labeling that A6's Censorship.md §8 cites: RL-1 (per-IP rate bound), RL-2 (HELLO-exempt liveness), RL-3 (flood-attack bandwidth dilution + Corollary RL-3.1 on linear-rather-than-amplified scaling), RL-4 (no false-positive denial). §9.1 explicit scope statement (OS / slowloris / spoofed-IP out-of-scope items); §9.2 `A_flood` adversary model with (a) RPC bandwidth exhaustion + (b) gossip channel crowding; §9.5 formal FA2 composition statement (RL-* tightens FA2's `(f/N)^{KR}` bound on Byzantine-flood-induced honest-message-loss without weakening union-tx-root admission); §9.6 operator-policy + NAT discussion. |

| [RateLimiterKeyDerivationSoundness.md](RateLimiterKeyDerivationSoundness.md) | Soundness of the S-014 token-bucket **bucket-KEY DERIVATION** function — the facet every prior S-014 proof abstracts as an opaque per-IP key (S014RateLimiterSoundness.md / S014RateLimiterDDOSResistance.md / S014ConcurrencyAnalysis.md / RateLimiterEviction.tla all reason *given* a correct key; this proof proves the key is correct). Audits the two derivation sites: RPC `key_rpc` = bare `addr_str(A)` no port + `"unknown"` fallback (`src/rpc/rpc.cpp:142-153`) and gossip `key_gossip` = `rfind(':')` port-strip of `Peer::address()=addr_str(A)+":"+port` (`src/net/gossip.cpp:148-154`, `src/net/peer.cpp:11-12`). Six lemmas L-1..L-6 (port-independence of both derivations; both are functions of the address alone and coincide; non-splitting one-host→one-key; `"unknown"` reachable only on a torn-down socket; **coalescing is monotone fail-safe**) + five theorems: T-1 (IPv4 per-host soundness — bounded by `⌊C+r·Δ⌋` regardless of ports/connections), T-2 (gossip same-host connection coalescing, composing with S026TcpKeepalive.md's live-connection bound), T-3 (`"unknown"` fallback creates no amplification + no cross-bucket denial; not adversary-selectable post-handshake), T-4 (IPv6 / zone-id `fe80::1%eth0` over-coalescing is fail-safe — the port is always the last colon-component so the strip never splits an IPv6 host across buckets), T-5 (RPC-vs-gossip key formats coincide AND own disjoint maps, so any asymmetry is benign). Central result: every derivation failure mode is a **coalescing** event (over-meters, never under-meters) because the key is a deterministic function of the source address (L-3) and a host has one address (L-4) — closing the end-to-end "a single host cannot exceed `⌊C+r·Δ⌋` per surface" claim that S014RateLimiterSoundness.md T-1 leaves resting on an unstated key-correctness premise. Adversary levers K1 (port rotation — defeated), K2 (prefix address rotation — out-of-derivation-layer, cross-ref DDoS A-V4 + deferred per-prefix bucketing), K3 (IPv6 hextet-strip — impossible), K4 (`"unknown"` poisoning — fail-safe). §6 threat matrix; §7 three advisory findings: F-1 (NAT-shared-IP fairness degradation — not a rate-bypass), F-2 (strip relies on `Peer::address()` unconditionally appending `:port` — discipline finding against a future IPv6-splitting regression), F-3 (no test pins the derivation directly — recommends a `test-rate-limiter-bucket` extension). No source change. References RFC 5952 (IPv6 text form), RFC 4007 (zone-id), RFC 6598 (CGN shared space), RFC 793/9293 (TCP source integrity). |
| [S031ConcurrencyComposition.md](S031ConcurrencyComposition.md) | S-031 six-layer concurrency-composition theorem covering the **chain-state mutation surface** (chain-state-layer companion to `S014ConcurrencyAnalysis.md`'s rate-limiter-layer companion). Six theorems T-1 (Mutual Exclusion of Applies — single `apply_block_locked` via `unique_lock<shared_mutex>` on `state_mutex_`) + T-2 (Read-Write Exclusion via shared_mutex — 11 read-only RPC handlers proceed N-way concurrently under `shared_lock`; writers via `unique_lock` exclude readers and other writers) + T-3 (Atomic Apply Semantics — A9 Phase 1 all-or-nothing `apply_transactions` via `StateSnapshot` capture + try/catch + `restore_state_snapshot` on throw; Phase 2A/2B lazy-capture amortizes TRANSFER-only blocks; Phase 2C `committed_state_view_` lock-free publish via `std::atomic_store`) + T-4 (Lazy-Snapshot Consistency — `serialize_state` under shared_lock produces a 10-namespace canonical snapshot at a single time-point per T-2 exclusion against writers) + T-5 (Async chain.save Soundness — dedicated `save_thread_` writes `.tmp` + atomic rename per POSIX/Win32 contract; coalesce-but-don't-drop via `save_pending_` flag + `save_mutex_`/`save_cv_`; crash window between apply and save is recovered via peer gossip) + T-6 (Gossip-Out-of-Lock v2.6 — every state-mutating RPC handler `lk.unlock()`s before `gossip_.broadcast`; slow peers cannot stall chain-state acquisition). | [AnonAddressDerivationMigration.md](AnonAddressDerivationMigration.md) | **OPEN decision-analysis** (C6 round 3) resolving the v1.0 `pubkey_form` address-derivation compat-break flagged by A5 in `SchemaDiscriminatorsImpl.md §4`. Documents the current `make_anon_address` formula (`"0x" + hex(pubkey)` — a reversible bijection, NOT a hash; `include/determ/types.hpp:153-155`), the §7.6.7 requirement that `pubkey_form` enter the address-derivation preimage, and why they conflict. Deep-analyzes the option space {A hash-based, B discriminator-prefix, C keep-current (rejected), D prefix+hash (dominated)} against three criteria (satisfies §7.6.7 / preserves pubkey-recoverability / fixed-length). **§4 crux verdict: the anon-tx verification path RECOVERS the sender pubkey from the `from` address via `parse_anon_pubkey` (confirmed at `validator.cpp:553-566` + `validator.cpp:1025-1042` COMPOSABLE_BATCH inner + `node.cpp:1916-1929` mempool admission); the pubkey is NOT carried separately in the tx — the `Transaction` struct (`block.hpp:205-221`) has no pubkey field.** Consequence: Option A (hash) is NOT a low-cost drop-in — it mandates a wire-format change (explicit `from_pubkey` field bound into `signing_bytes()` + a `make_anon_address(from_pubkey)==from` consistency check at all three verify sites + emission in `light/sign_tx.cpp` + `wallet/main.cpp`), whereas Option B preserves recoverability and needs no wire change but yields permanent variable-length addresses. | [LightClientArchiveSoundness.md](LightClientArchiveSoundness.md) | Offline-reverifiable header-archive soundness proof (C7 round 3) for the `export-headers` (B3 round 2) → `verify-archive` (C3 round 3) flow: an archive that passes `verify-archive` against a pinned genesis is a cryptographically sound attestation of the chain's header sequence over `[from, from+count)`, re-checkable indefinitely with no live daemon. the export step **fails closed** on any header signed by a non-`K_0` creator (writes no archive on committee drift — a positive safety property), so an archive is sound for committee-stable ranges out of the box, while cross-rotation ranges require an operator-supplied extended committee fed identically to both `export-headers` and `verify-archive` since neither derives rotation from the chain; the same limitation `LightClientThreatModel.md` §6.5 + F-1 record for the online pipeline). §4.5 supporting lemmas AR-L1..AR-L3 (archive↔`rpc_headers`-envelope reconstruction, genesis-recompute online/offline identity, digest binding). §5 composition: AR-1 composes with T-L1 (genesis anchor) + T-L2 (committee-sig trust) — the archive applies the same two cryptographic walls to archive bytes rather than live RPC replies; §5.2 sketches the future AR-1 + **MT-4** (`MerkleTreeSoundness.md` offline Merkle-inclusion) → offline state-membership composition; §5.4 gives the online (T-Lx) ↔ archive (AR-x) cross-walk. §6 known limitations: AR-3 range-completeness (the big one), committee-rotation tracking, no freshness guarantee, stripped archives not offline-self-verifying for committee sigs. Cryptographic assumptions: A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA), A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance, `Preliminaries.md` §2.1), A3 (SHA-256 preimage); no new primitive. Cross-references `LightClientThreatModel.md` (the online per-invocation pipeline this archive flow reuses), `MerkleTreeSoundness.md` (MT-4 offline inclusion primitive), `Safety.md` (FA1), `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` (state_root surface for the future §5.2 composition), `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md`. Test surface: `tools/test_light_verify_archive.sh` (17 assertions — offline re-verification round-trip) + the `export-headers` regressions. |
| [AccountHistorySoundness.md](AccountHistorySoundness.md) | Trustless verified balance/nonce **trajectory** soundness for the `determ-light account-history` flow (D3 R40) — a verified sequence of `(height, balance, nonce)` rows for one account sampled across a height range `[H1, H2]` at stride `S`, where **every row is independently anchored** to the operator's pinned genesis by the same per-invocation machinery `LightClientThreatModel.md` proves for a single point. Four theorems AH-1 (per-point soundness — if a row is emitted, its value is `D`'s genuine on-chain state at that height; defeats forged-value / stale-or-forked-proof / unsigned-`state_root` strategies cryptographically by composing T-L2 committee-sig + MT-4/T-L3 state-proof + T-L1 genesis anchor; bound `K·2⁻¹²⁸ + log₂(leaf_count)·2⁻¹²⁸ + 2⁻¹²⁸` per sampled height) + AH-2 (trajectory consistency — each row binds the `state_root` from ITS OWN committee-verified `header[h]`; no shared root across rows, so a daemon cannot make `h_i`'s proof validate against `h_j`'s root; the cross-height-confusion attack reduces to an A2 collision) + AH-3 (**nonce monotonicity is necessary-not-sufficient** — a daemon serving an internally-consistent forged history could preserve monotonicity, so monotonicity is a defense-in-depth *cross-check*, NOT a soundness source; AH-1's per-point committee-sig anchoring is the real guarantee; balance has no monotonicity property at all, reinforcing that per-point anchoring is the universal guarantee) + AH-4 (sampling-gap honesty — the trajectory proves the values AT the sampled heights only; balance can move up-and-back within a `--step` gap unobserved; a verified *sample at stride `S`*, not a continuous audit — the temporal-sampling analog of `LightClientArchiveSoundness.md` AR-3's range honesty). Adds NO new cryptographic assumption — the *temporal composition* of T-L1 + T-L2 + T-L3/MT-4 re-applied per sampled height (AH-1 = `LightClientThreatModel.md` T-L4 at a fixed historical height). Honest about the shipped head-only-state-proof constraint: each sampled height's committee-signed `state_root` is header-verified, but balance/nonce are Merkle-verified at HEAD only (the daemon's `state_proof`/`account` RPCs are head-only; rows annotated `balance_proven_at_height` + `balance_merkle_verified`, the latter true only when the sample is the head); §6.4 records this as a daemon-capability availability question orthogonal to AH-1 soundness (which conditions on *emission*), and the height-generic code auto-upgrades if the RPC gains a height param. §6.2 records the static genesis-committee `K_0` limitation (cross-rotation ranges fail closed; need an operator-supplied extended committee) inherited from AR-4. Composes T-L4 (`LightClientThreatModel.md`) + MT-4 (`MerkleTreeSoundness.md`) + FA-Apply-3 nonce-monotonicity (`NonceMonotonicity.md`, the chain-side invariant AH-3 cross-checks against) + FA1 (`Safety.md` §7). Cross-references A1/A2/A3 per `Preliminaries.md` §2.0 (no FA3-for-SHA). Test surface: `tools/test_light_account_history.sh` (6 assertions — D3 R40 cluster-bound; per-sampled-row verify, wrong-height-proof reject, monotonicity-violation surfaced, sampling-gap documented). |
| [StateRootAnchorSoundness.md](StateRootAnchorSoundness.md) | Per-height committee-verified `state_root` anchor soundness (F6 R40) for the `determ-light verify-state-root --height H` subcommand (F3 this round) — the single load-bearing trust hinge every trust-minimized account read consumes: the committee-verified `state_root` at one height `H`, bound to the operator's pinned genesis. Five theorems SR-1 (committee-anchored root — the reported `state_root(H)` is committee-committed, not daemon-asserted; **via the transitive-forward digest link**, NOT a direct digest signature — see below; bound `≤ (K+1)·2⁻¹²⁸`) + SR-2 (genesis-binding / no floating header — the prev_hash walk from the genesis-anchored block 0 up to `H` defeats the isolated-committee-signed-forked-header attack; bound `≤ (H·K+1)·2⁻¹²⁸`) + SR-3 (height-binding — `B.index` is the first field of `compute_block_digest`, so the substituted-height attack costs an A1 forgery or A2 collision; bound `≤ K·2⁻¹²⁸`) + SR-4 (fail-closed — any sig failure / chain break / genesis mismatch / malformed header / absent successor exits non-zero with a structured diagnostic, never a bare daemon-reported root; the per-command instance of LightClientThreatModel L-6) + SR-5 (pre-S-033 vacuity honesty — on a chain where every header's `state_root == 0`, the binding is **vacuous** (the zero-skip shim contributes nothing to `signing_bytes`); the command reports the absence rather than emitting a meaningless zero root, mirroring `read_account_trustless`'s `"chain has not activated state_root (S-033)"` throw). **Load-bearing binding finding (§3, grounded in source): `state_root` is NOT in `compute_block_digest`** (what the K-of-K committee directly Ed25519-signs — that carries `index, prev_hash, tx_root, delay_seed, consensus_mode, bft_proposer, creators, creator_tx_lists, creator_ed_sigs, creator_dh_inputs`); `state_root` is bound into `Block::signing_bytes` / `block_hash` (when non-zero, the S-033 zero-skip shim) and is committee-certified **transitively forward** via `state_root(H) ∈ signing_bytes(H) ∈ block_hash(H) = prev_hash(H+1) ∈ digest(H+1)` — so a committee signature on the *successor* block `H+1` certifies `H`'s `state_root`. (Contrast: `tx_root` IS directly in the digest — see `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md`.) §3.4 documents the head-block boundary honestly: the head's `state_root` has no signed successor yet, so it is certified only once a successor block is signed (full nodes enforce it meanwhile via the apply-layer S-033 gate); §6.4 records the `verify_headers`-trusts-reported-`block_hash` defense-in-depth hardening. Proves `determ-light verify-state-root` (F3 R40); composes `LightClientThreatModel.md` T-L2 (committee-sig trust) + T-L4 (the factored-out anchor) + the block-digest binding + `MerkleTreeSoundness.md` §5.4's chain-of-trust prefix; SR-1 is the per-height sub-lemma `AccountHistorySoundness.md` AH-1 consumes per sample. Assumptions A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA), A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance), transitively A3 (preimage, T-L1 genesis case); per `Preliminaries.md` §2.0 — explicitly NOT FA3-for-SHA. Cross-references `light/verify_state_root.cpp` (`verify_state_root_at`) + `light/main.cpp::cmd_verify_state_root`, `light/verify.cpp::light_compute_block_digest`/`verify_headers`/`verify_block_sigs`, `src/node/producer.cpp::compute_block_digest`, `src/chain/block.cpp::signing_bytes`/`compute_hash`, `light/trustless_read.cpp::read_account_trustless` (the in-tree composite F3 factors out). Test surface: `tools/test_light_verify_state_root.sh` (7 assertions — F3 R40 cluster-bound; wrong-genesis fail, tampered-`state_root`-at-`H`-with-valid-digest-sigs fail via the `H+1` link, pre-S-033 reports "S-033 not active"). |
| [StakeDistributionMetrics.md](StakeDistributionMetrics.md) | Decentralization-metric correctness for `tools/operator_stake_distribution.sh` (Nakamoto + Gini). **Arithmetic-correctness + interpretation** proof, not cryptographic. Four theorems SD-1 (Nakamoto integer-exactness — the script's `3·cumulative > total` integer test equals the real-valued `cumulative > total/3` exactly, with NO floating-point boundary error and correct strict-`>` handling of the exact-`1/3` tie, by cross-multiplying through `mult > 0`; also dispatches the `T//3` integer-truncation trap) + SD-2 (Nakamoto monotonicity / well-definedness — descending-accumulation is greedy-optimal for fewest-entities-to-exceed-threshold via an exchange argument; edge cases single-validator→1, all-equal→`⌊n/3⌋+1`, zero-total→0, empty→0 all match the implementation) + SD-3 (Gini bounds + sorted-form correctness — the script's sorted-form `G = Σᵢ(2i−n−1)x₍ᵢ₎/(n·Σx)` equals the double-sum definition `Σᵢⱼ|xᵢ−xⱼ|/(2nΣx)` by the standard sign-counting derivation; `0 ≤ G ≤ 1−1/n < 1`; `G=0 ⟺` all stakes equal; `n<2`/`T=0`→`None`) + SD-4 (read-only soundness — only the `status` + `stakes` RPCs; no chain mutation; exit code reflects RPC health + arg validity alone). §4 reproduces the fixture (`tools/test_operator_stake_distribution.sh`: stakes 4000/3000/2500/2000/1500, total 13000 → Nakamoto 2 via `3·4000=12000 ≤ 13000` then `3·7000=21000 > 13000`; Gini = 12000/65000 ≈ 0.18, cross-checked against the double-sum form). §5 interpretation caveat: under K-of-K MD-mode safety is unconditional in `f` (`Safety.md` T-1) so the Nakamoto coefficient is **decentralization-informational, NOT a live safety threshold**; the `1/3` reading approximates a real bound only under BFT-escalation (`f_h < |K_h|/3`, `Preliminaries.md` §3.3 / FA5), and even there as a stake-weighted proxy composing with FA6 slashing + S-010/S-011 stake-pricing. | [ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md](ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md) | Trustless cross-shard `i:`-receipt-membership soundness (R41 I6) for `determ-light verify-receipt-inclusion` — the `i:`-namespace sibling of TxInclusionProofSoundness (tx) and StakeProofSoundness (s:). Five theorems RI-1 (committee-signed state_root binds the i: leaf via the transitive-forward signing_bytes/S-033 chain + K-of-K sigs, reducing to A1/A2; invokes StateRootAnchorSoundness SR-1..SR-3) + RI-2 (Merkle state-proof for the presence-marker leaf is sound — MT-1/MT-2/MT-3/MT-4, with MT-2 leaf-key domain separation **load-bearing** because the i: value-hash is the CONSTANT `SHA256(0x01)`: all receipt identity lives in the Merkle KEY `"i:"+src_be8+tx_hash`, not a value decode) + RI-3 (one-sided verifier — non-application is NOT provable under MT-5; withheld/`not_found` → UNVERIFIABLE, never a false NOT-APPLIED) + RI-4 (S-040 leaf_count caller-trust) + RI-5 (fail-closed exit). Composes to RI-E ≤ 2⁻⁹². **Shipped end-to-end:** the daemon's `state_proof` RPC now serves the composite-key `i:` namespace via R-ext (the caller hex-encodes the binary key body `u64_be(src)‖tx_hash`, the daemon hex-decodes + length-checks + prepends `i:`; raw bytes can't ride a JSON string since a SHA-256 hash breaks UTF-8 `dump()`). An applied receipt yields a real INCLUDED (Merkle-verified against the committee-signed `state_root`), a never-applied key yields NOT-INCLUDED (`not_found`); UNVERIFIABLE only vs. a legacy daemon or on tamper. | [CrossShardRelaySoundness.md](CrossShardRelaySoundness.md) | Cross-shard receipt relay + untrusted-buffer staging soundness (CR-1..CR-7): the transport layer from a finalized source block, through the beacon relay re-broadcast, into the destination shard's untrusted `pending_inbound_receipts_` buffer (`node.cpp::on_cross_shard_receipt_bundle`) carries ZERO trust — relaying/buffering/deduping/dropping a bundle cannot credit an account, inflate supply, or affect any finalized state. Beacon relay is state-pure (CR-1), role-dispatch is an exhaustive BEACON/SHARD/SINGLE trichotomy with only SHARD buffering (CR-2), buffer dedup by `(src_shard, tx_hash)` is advisory while the canonical no-double-credit is the downstream V13 + `applied_inbound_receipts_` (CR-3, A2), the safety gate is the downstream K-of-K source-block ratification + V12/V13 + finalized apply — buffering is necessary-but-not-sufficient and a forged bundle dies in the buffer unless K honest source-committee signatures back it (CR-4, A1, locating where FA7 L-7.4's gate actually runs), the `Buf`/`Seen` first-seen maps co-insert/co-erase under one lock so the S-016 latency gate is well-defined (CR-5), the buffer is excluded from the 10 S-033 namespaces + the snapshot so buffer divergence cannot fork `state_root` — the precise reason S-016's divergence was latency-only (CR-6, A2), and the receive holds `state_mutex_` across role-dispatch + mutation (CR-7, composes S-031). | [StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md](StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md) | Soundness of the **daemon-side** composite-key `state_proof` RPC extension (the `i:`/`m:`/`p:` branch of `Node::rpc_state_proof`, `src/node/node.cpp:3406-3432`) — the upstream complement of `ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md`'s verifier-side `i:` read. Three theorems + one lemma: **SP-CK-1** (byte-exact reconstruction — the daemon rebuilds the leaf key `"<ns>:"+body` byte-for-byte identically to `Chain::build_state_leaves` for each composite encoding `i:`=`u64_be(src)‖tx_hash` (40B) / `m:`=`u32_be(shard)` (4B) / `p:`=`u64_be(eff)‖u32_be(idx)` (12B), both sides running `for(i=7..0/3..0)` big-endian, so a served proof targets the intended leaf or `nullopt`; unconditional deterministic-function-equality, no crypto assumption; doubles as the regression tripwire guarding the two hand-rolled packing sites) + **SP-CK-2** (length-check completeness — the exact-width gate `body.size()!=want` (40/4/12) plus the `from_hex` `try/catch` reject every malformed body BEFORE `Chain::state_proof` is reached, with structured `invalid hex key` / `composite key wrong length` diagnostics and no aliasing or out-of-bounds; no-aliasing leans on `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` T-2 byte-0 namespace disjointness so a correct-length body in the wrong namespace cannot cross-alias) + **SP-CK-3** (sourcing-independent soundness — under fully-Byzantine `A_daemon`, whether `key_bytes` is daemon-rebuilt (R-ext) or client-built (R-cli), the verifier re-derives the leaf hash from the returned `key_bytes` (parsed at `light/verify.cpp:349-350`; `determ::crypto::merkle_verify`, called at `light/verify.cpp:378-380`, recomputes `merkle_leaf_hash(key_bytes, value_hash)` internally at `src/crypto/merkle.cpp:140`) and gates on the committee-signed root, so a wrong-key proof fails root-equality by MT-4; the daemon's reconstruction is a *convenience, not a trust assumption*, and R-cli is strictly stronger — the daemon-side complement of `ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md` RI-2; reduces to A2, adding zero new assumptions over the simple-key reads). Lemma **SP-CK-T** (hex-transport necessity + losslessness — a 32-byte SHA-256 `tx_hash` is negligibly-rarely valid UTF-8, so raw bytes throw `nlohmann::json::dump()` `type_error.316`; hex makes the body `dump()`-safe ASCII, and `from_hex∘to_hex=id` (types.hpp:61-82) is an exact bijection — so hex is required, not stylistic, and introduces no key ambiguity). §5 composition lattice: SP-CK-1/SP-CK-2 unconditional, SP-CK-3 reduces to A2 via `MerkleTreeSoundness.md` MT-4 underneath `StateRootAnchorSoundness.md` SR-1, feeding `ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md` RI-1..RI-5. §6 findings: F-1 (reconstruction equality implementation-pinned not type-enforced; shared-helper refactor tracked), F-2 (width-check sufficiency modulo T-2 disjointness invariant), F-3 (membership-only / MT-5 one-sided boundary), F-4 (head-only `state_root`). | [NegativeVerdictSoundness.md](NegativeVerdictSoundness.md) | Soundness asymmetry of the `NOT-INCLUDED` / absence verdict across the `determ-light` verifier family — the dual of the inclusion proofs, taken as its own subject for the first time. Splits the family into two regimes with different trust footings for their *negatives*: the **block-body regime** (`verify-tx-inclusion`) recomputes `tx_root` from the full body and enforces a body↔committee-signed-set bijection (`light/verify_tx_inclusion.cpp:184-255`), so its `NOT-INCLUDED` is a **cryptographically sound exclusion** (reduces to **A2**; lifts `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md` TI-2); the **state-proof regime** (`verify-receipt-inclusion` `i:`, `verify-merge-state` `m:`, `verify-param-change` `p:`) reports `NOT-INCLUDED` on a daemon's bare `state_proof` `not_found`, but the sorted-leaves primitive has **no non-membership proof** (`MerkleTreeSoundness.md` MT-5), so that negative is **NOT cryptographically backed** — `A_daemon` forges it unconditionally by withholding a genuinely-committed leaf. Six theorems + one lemma: NV-1 (block-body negative sound, bound `(K+1)·2⁻¹²⁸`) + NV-2 (state-proof negative unsound — constructive withholding attack, forgery prob `1`) + NV-3 (names the exact non-cryptographic premise **(H-neg)** negative-honesty that the state-proof negative rests on, outside the {A1,A2,A3} base and discharged by neither the genesis anchor nor committee-sig trust) + NV-4 (no negative→positive weaponization — the `not_found` and positive branches are mutually exclusive via the outer `if (error)` short-circuit, so an unsound negative cannot manufacture a false `INCLUDED`/`APPLIED` settlement; confines the harm to the fail-safe withhold/retry direction) + NV-5 / NV-5a (fail-closed `UNVERIFIABLE` on any non-literal-`not_found` refusal; the `not_found`→`NOT-INCLUDED` branch is reachable only for the exact locally-built canonical key — `i:` `:1440-1444`, `m:` `:1770-1777`, `p:` `:2125-2133`) + NV-6 (caller contract: a state-proof `NOT-INCLUDED` MUST be treated as "no membership proof obtained" ≈ `UNVERIFIABLE` for value-affecting decisions and MUST NOT be treated as authoritative absence; the block-body `NOT-INCLUDED` MAY be; necessary-and-sufficient for downstream `C`'s soundness) + lemma NV-T (enumerability dichotomy — the block-body set is fully reconstructable from one committee-signed object; the head-only `state_proof` leaf set is not; enumerability is the structural discriminator). Corollary NV-6.1 shows `i:` append-only stability rescues the *positive*, not the negative. §10 concrete-security table isolates the single row (`state_proof` negative, footing A1+A2+**(H-neg)**) that is not purely cryptographic. Findings F-1 (source-comment refinement), F-2 (additive `negative_footing` JSON field), F-3 (SMT-migration / multi-peer upgrade path that would make the state-proof negative sound), F-4 (NV-1 composition guard tied to `validator.cpp:161-167` + `producer.cpp:612`). Assumptions **A1**/**A2**/**A3** (`Preliminaries.md` §2.0); adversary `A_daemon`. The negative-verdict complement to `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md` (TI-2), `ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md` (RI-3), `StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md` (SP-CK-3), and the applied consequence of `MerkleTreeSoundness.md` MT-5 at the verifier-and-caller layer; supplies the per-command *negative-verdict* column `LightClientCompositionMap.md` §5 leaves implicit. Cross-references `MerkleTreeSoundness.md` MT-5, `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md`, `ReceiptInclusionProofSoundness.md`, `StateProofCompositeKeySoundness.md`, `LightClientThreatModel.md` (L-6 / `A_daemon`), `LightClientCompositionMap.md`, `CrossShardReceiptDedup.md` T-R7, `S036UnderQuorumMerge.md`, `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-033/§S-040, `docs/PROTOCOL.md` §10.2. |
| [MultiPeerCrossCheckSoundness.md](MultiPeerCrossCheckSoundness.md) | Soundness of the `determ-light cross-check` multi-peer divergence detector (commit `36e7053`) — closes the single-daemon limitation flagged across the light-client family (`LightClientCompositionMap.md` §6, `LightClientThreatModel.md` §6). Given ≥2 daemon endpoints + a pinned genesis, each peer is independently committee-verified from genesis to head (`anchor_genesis` T-L1 + `verify_chain_to_head` T-L2), then peers sharing a height must agree on `(block_hash, state_root)`. **MPC-1** (divergence-soundness — no false positive: two honest daemons on the canonical chain are byte-identical at every shared height under A1+A2, so DIVERGENCE against honest daemons is never raised; a DIVERGENCE verdict implies either ≥f+1 committee equivocation or an A1/A2 break, prob ≤ `(H·K+1)·2⁻¹²⁸`) + **MPC-2** (a DIVERGENCE is a transferable equivocation witness feeding FA6 — the across-peers observable of the FA1 §5.3 / S-030-D2 two-instance condition) + **MPC-3** (lag-benignity — a behind peer is not compared, no false DIVERGENCE from async heights) + **MPC-4** (fail-closed — a peer failing its own anchor/committee verify → UNVERIFIABLE before any comparison, never a false AGREE) + **MPC-5** (per-peer guarantee preserved — each peer fully verified before comparison; adds detection, weakens nothing). Both localhost (`--rpc-port`) and cross-host (`--peer <host:port>`, via `RpcClient`'s getaddrinfo path — commit `9fed9ad`) peers are supported. Honest limitations: all-peers-collude is silent (needs ≥1 *independent* honest peer — cross-host raises the bar but the operator still chooses the host set); not a non-membership/liveness proof. Assumptions A1+A2 (no new assumption over per-peer `verify-chain`); adversaries `A_eclipse` / `A_byz_committee`. Verdicts AGREE/DIVERGENCE/INCONCLUSIVE/UNVERIFIABLE (exit 0/2/3/1). Test surface `tools/test_light_cross_check.sh` (offline CLI contract deterministic; live 2-daemon AGREE cluster-bound). | [LightStatePersistenceSoundness.md](LightStatePersistenceSoundness.md) | Soundness of the `determ-light` persisted-anchor cache (`verify-chain --persist` + `state --show/--clear/--selftest` + `light/persist.{hpp,cpp}`) — lands the *stateful sync client* substrate the medium-tier light-client scope deferred and the limitation `LightClientCompositionMap.md` §6 records as "no persistence (re-anchors from genesis every run)". `LightState = {schema_version, genesis_hash, head_height, head_block_hash, head_state_root}`. Six theorems: **LSP-1** (no-unverified-write — `cmd_verify_chain` writes only on the success path AFTER `anchor_genesis` + `verify_chain_to_head`, so a persisted anchor is always a committee-verified head, never a daemon-asserted one; a failed/unreachable verify leaves no file) + **LSP-2** (genesis-pin on reuse — the persisted `genesis_hash` is the LOCAL recompute, re-checked against the operator's `--genesis` on resume; a state from a different chain is rejected — the persisted analog of T-L1) + **LSP-3** (schema-version gate — `schema_version ≠ 1` rejected, never misread) + **LSP-4** (fail-closed load — malformed JSON / missing / short-or-non-hex field throws → exit 1, distinct from exit-0 graceful absence; `head_state_root` empty allowed ONLY for the pre-S-033 case) + **LSP-5** (read-soundness — anything `load_light_state` returns is well-formed, schema-current, and (if this client wrote it) committee-verified; the cache cannot inject an unverified/wrong-chain head) + **LSP-6** (resume-soundness — SHIPPED, commit `22c04fa`: `verify-chain --resume` consumes the cached anchor and verifies ONLY the suffix above it, skipping the committee-signed prefix; re-pins genesis (LSP-2) + falls back to a full verify on absent/corrupt/wrong-chain/not-ahead, never weaker; a fork below the anchor is a HARD error. Prefix-skip is sound because each suffix block's K-of-K sig binds index+prev_hash, so the first suffix block's `prev_hash == cached head_block_hash` transitively re-validates the skipped prefix under A1+A2 — see `VerifyChainWalkSoundness.md`. A pre-merge adversarial verifier caught an index-0 diversion attack; closed by the index-contiguity gate + the `verify_headers` anchored-page guard). Trust model: trusted local environment (`LightClientThreatModel.md` §6) — a locally-tampered file is OUT of scope (a local attacker editing it can edit the binary); the genesis pin + forward re-verify, not file integrity, are the defense. No new assumption over per-run `verify-chain` {A1, A2}. The LSP-2 gate is a concrete offline subcommand — `state --verify-anchor --genesis <file>` recomputes `compute_genesis_hash` locally and returns PASS / MISMATCH(exit 2). Test surface `tools/test_light_state.sh` (27 offline assertions: `--selftest` round-trip + 5 reject paths, `--show`/`--clear`/`--show --json` (present/head_height/age_seconds; fail-closed-on-corrupt under --json)/env-override contract, `--verify-anchor` PASS/MISMATCH/usage gates, `--persist`/`--resume` arg + no-write-on-failed-verify; cluster-bound live `--persist` write + live LSP-6 resume + live LSP-7 monotonicity legs on WSL2/CI). LSP-7 (head monotonicity — a daemon below the cached committee-verified anchor is REFUSED, at-anchor must present the cached block; the pre-LSP-7 silent full-verify fail-open is closed) is source-guarded offline by `tools/test_light_resume_monotonicity_guard.sh` (SELFTEST-backed). Machine-checkable companion `tla/LightStatePersistence.tla` (FB57, models the resume consumer via ResumeVerify + INV_ResumeSound/NoFalseAccept). Cross-references `LightClientThreatModel.md` §6, `LightClientCompositionMap.md` §6, `MultiPeerCrossCheckSoundness.md`, `VerifyChainWalkSoundness.md`, `StateRootAnchorSoundness.md`, `Preliminaries.md` §2.0–§2.2. |
| [VerifyChainWalkSoundness.md](VerifyChainWalkSoundness.md) | Soundness of the SHARED page-walk core `light/trustless_read.cpp::verify_chain_walk` — the function both `verify_chain_to_head` (from-genesis, start_from=0) and `verify_chain_from_anchor` (resume, start_from=anchor_height) call; the walk-layer companion to `LightStatePersistenceSoundness.md` LSP-6 (cache layer) + `LightClientThreatModel.md` T-L2. | [CrossBinaryCanonicalFormat.md](CrossBinaryCanonicalFormat.md) | Structural soundness of CROSS-BINARY canonical-format agreement — WHY `determ`, `determ-wallet`, and `determ-light` compute byte-identical canonical forms (Transaction `signing_bytes`/`tx_hash`, Block `compute_hash`/digest, genesis hash, anon-address derivation). **CBF-1** (single-implementation structural equivalence — each canonical form has exactly ONE `src/` definition; `determ` links it directly while `determ-light` links the SAME `src/chain/*.cpp` via the explicit non-glob CMake reuse list `CMakeLists.txt:262-282`, and `determ-wallet` re-implements the tx layout inline `wallet/main.cpp:8224-8244`/`:9543-9562` byte-for-byte — so agreement is by construction/relink, not coincidence) + **CBF-2** (the light-client's verification soundness DEPENDS on this — `light/verify.cpp::light_compute_block_digest` + `light/sign_tx.cpp::compute_signing_bytes` are the re-implementation surfaces that must stay byte-identical to the daemon, the single divergence-risk the parity tests guard; cross-ref FB56 digest binding) + **CBF-3** (the runtime parity tests `tools/test_cross_binary_tx_parity.sh` — 3-binary `tx_hash` byte-equality across `determ tx-hash` / `determ-wallet tx-sign-verify` / `determ-light sign-tx` — are the empirical proof the build actually relinked the shared modules) + **CBF-4** (boundary: a STRUCTURAL/build-time guarantee that the binaries AGREE, NOT a cryptographic proof that the format is sound — that is the per-format proofs' job). Assumptions: a correct from-one-tree build; adversary = a silent build/codec divergence. Test surface `tools/test_cross_binary_tx_parity.sh` (29 offline, every-host — signing_bytes/tx_hash only, no genesis-hash leg) + the `determ test-*-determinism` suites. | [CanonicalSigningBytesParity.md](CanonicalSigningBytesParity.md) | **FB61** — byte-identity of the Transaction `signing_bytes` pre-image across all FOUR implementations (the per-pre-image byte-identity discharge of CBF-2's Transaction mirror in `CrossBinaryCanonicalFormat.md`, which proves only the structural-reuse regime). States CSP precisely: for any `T=(type,from,to,amount,fee,nonce,payload)`, `chain_SB = wallet_tsv_SB = wallet_cold_SB = light_SB = SB(T) = u8(type)‖from‖0x00‖to‖0x00‖u64_be(amount)‖u64_be(fee)‖u64_be(nonce)‖payload`, hence an identical `SHA256(SB)=tx_hash` and Ed25519 sig interop across `determ`/`determ-wallet`/`determ-light`. Field-by-field layout table (offset/width/encoding/source line). **T-1** canonical defines the spec (`src/chain/block.cpp:17-29` build, `:31-34` hash; struct order `block.hpp:206-212`); **T-2** wallet `tx-sign-verify` == spec (`wallet/main.cpp:8228-8242`, SHA256 `:8248-8249`); **T-3** wallet `cold-sign` == spec (`wallet/main.cpp:9550-9560`, SHA256 `:9564-9565`); **T-4** light == spec restricted to empty payload (`light/sign_tx.cpp:37-62`; payload omission `:50`/no insert after `:60`) — safe-by-construction because the light sign-tx CLI has NO payload parameter (`compute_signing_bytes` takes no payload arg; `sign_light_tx` emits `payload=""` at `:118`), so the restriction is TOTAL over the light API's tx set. Each proof obligation ("source token sequence == canonical token sequence") is discharged by inspection AND mechanically by the source guard. The byte-identity equalities are UNCONDITIONAL (pure straight-line transcription, (P-det)+(P-be)); A2 used only for §6's divergence-DETECTION direction, A1 only for the interop corollary's message-argument equality. **Mechanized witnesses (defense-in-depth):** source guard `tools/test_signing_bytes_source_parity.sh` (pre-build, 4-site token-parity, SELFTEST negative control) + runtime `tools/test_cross_binary_tx_parity.sh` (post-build 3-binary `tx_hash` equality + `valid=true` sig interop, tamper negative control) + edge runtime `tools/test_cross_binary_tx_parity_edge.sh` (high-byte / u64-max field values + the wallet's 2nd/3rd `signing_bytes` copies `cold-sign`/`sign-anon-tx`). Threat: a one-line drift (flipped endianness, moved NUL, reordered field) silently breaks tx interop (a tx signed by one binary fails verify on another) and, since `tx_hash` is the `tx_root` leaf, breaks inclusion proofs too. Companion to `CrossBinaryCanonicalFormat.md`, `TxInclusionProofSoundness.md`, `LightClientCompositionMap.md`; reduces to A1 + A2 (interop/detection only). |
| [BlockDigestCrossBinaryParity.md](BlockDigestCrossBinaryParity.md) | **FB62** — byte-identity of the light client's block-digest recompute (`light/verify.cpp::light_compute_block_digest`) vs the daemon's authoritative `src/node/producer.cpp::compute_block_digest` on every NON-F2 block (the digest-layer sibling of FB61 CanonicalSigningBytesParity; the byte-identity discharge of CBF-2's `light_compute_block_digest` re-implementation surface; consumes the field model of `S030-D2-Analysis.md`). Side-by-side field-order table for BOTH functions: the core 10 fields identical (`producer.cpp:610-620 ≡ verify.cpp:59-69`), the three F2 roots present in producer only (inbound `producer.cpp:629-635`, eq `:650-655`, abort `:656-661` — light has none), and the `partner_subset_hash` (`producer.cpp:674-676 ≡ verify.cpp:76-78`) + `timestamp` (`producer.cpp:689-691 ≡ verify.cpp:88-90`) conditional tail identical (same order, same trigger). **T-1** producer defines the spec (the digest the committee actually signs, `producer.cpp:608-693`); **T-2** light == spec on the non-F2 domain — the omitted F2 roots are absent there, so the remaining sequences coincide; discharged by the token-sequence equality (source guard) + the conditional-trigger equality (the partner `is_zero_hash_`/`!= zero` and the syntactically-identical `!creator_proposer_times.empty()` timestamp gates); **T-3** fail-closed soundness — on an F2 / cross-shard block (non-empty inbound or non-zero eq/abort view roots) light omits roots the producer bound, so `light_digest != producer_digest`, so EVERY committee sig fails light's check: a false NEGATIVE (UNVERIFIABLE), never a false positive (documented contract `verify.cpp:40-56` — verify those against a full node). The byte equality is UNCONDITIONAL ((P-det) determinism + (P-app) same `SHA256Builder` over the same linked `Block`); A1 lifts digest equality to sig-verify equivalence, A2 only for the divergence-DETECTION direction. **Mechanized witnesses (defense-in-depth):** NEW source guard `tools/test_block_digest_xbinary_parity.sh` (static, pre-build, asserts core-identical + light == producer minus 3 F2 roots + partner/timestamp tail same order/gates; `SELFTEST=1` liveness with reorder/drop/spurious-F2/core-reorder drift classes) + producer fence `tools/test_block_digest.sh` (in-process: conditional appendages fire only on trigger, bound-field mutation changes the digest) + cluster end-to-end `tools/test_light_verify_block_sigs.sh` (real block 1, all K sigs verify against the light recompute; tamper negative control). Coverage split: cluster pins the common (non-merged) case at runtime; source guard pins the conditional merged/reconciled tail the cluster's block 1 never triggers. Threat: a tail drift makes the light client reject valid merged-block sigs (light-client availability loss) or, dually, a producer-side tail bug lets two distinct merged blocks share a digest (FA1 equivocation-binding loss); cross-ref `S030-D2-Analysis.md`. Companion to `CanonicalSigningBytesParity.md` (FB61), `CrossBinaryCanonicalFormat.md`, `Safety.md` (FA1), `LightClientThreatModel.md`/`LightClientCompositionMap.md`; reduces to A1 + A2 (lift/detection only). |
